Okauro
is a character in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
.
Background
An armored Huana turns and looks you up and down. She holds this motionless pose across a long and contemplative silence.
Finally she draws out a single pire and balances the coin on her knuckles.
Okauro is different from other bounty hunter fixers in that she ascribes an almost mystical value to the act of trading heads for coin. However, that also means that she honors every contract - or coin bond - to the letter. Part of it comes from the fact that she's a paladin of the Goldpact order. Part from the fact that her zeal has given her an almost perfect work attendance record.
Oh, and she also enjoys knitting. Occasionally.
Interactions
Okauro can be found on the top level of the
Sacred Stair
, near the center of the area.
This character
starts
quests
.
Bounty - Dhwrgas the Ascetic
Bounty - Onadere the Siren
Bounty - Ikorno
Bounty - Urnox the Rathun
This character has
other interactions
.
A Watcher with the
Goldpact Knights
Paladin
subclass, or the Mercenary
background
can choose some additional dialogue choices when you first meet her.
You can try snatch the coin from her with
Sleight of Hand
7, either way she manages to keep hold of it. She then places the coin in the palm of your hand, and you gain
1
.
Quests
Okauro is a
bounty
fixer.
Behind the scenes
Okauro uses two conversation portraits. The portrait above is used during her introductory dialogue (and is unique to her), and the one below is used for all other instances. This is likely an oversight on part of the developers.
Gallery
Okauro's other portrait

is a character in

Background
A Rauataian native, originating from a territory conquered long ago by the kingdom, the peddler trades wares as a citizen of the Great Kingdom. She's never known anything else and grew accustomed to Rauataian rule, like her parents and grandparents. NPC_SD_Orron
GUID
1008901c-94ff-4d2c-a582-5092f6283bce
Orron
is a character in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
.
Background
A dwarf sits before a generous and curious spread - steamed mussels arranged in concentric circles, rounds of flatbread stacked in a neat tower, and melon sliced in even triangles.
Yet his attention is focused on the four cups and the bottle in front of him.
He has the cups organized in an almost perfect square around the bottle, but as you look on, he leans down to adjust one.
The others with him wait quietly and observe the ritual.
Holding his breath, he takes the bottle and measures an equal serving of wine into the cups, making three or four passes over each.
His companions look on with practiced patience.
At last the bottle is empty, and he places it in the exact center of the square.
He picks it up and puts it down in the same spot twice more before he's satisfied.
Orron leads a squad of
Goldpact Knights
fresh off a contract with the
VTC
, for protecting one of their most valuable properties - the
Luminous Adra Mill
. They are now bound for
Takowa
for another contract with
Rauatai
.
Interactions
This character is
involved in
quests
.
All Aboard
This character has
other interactions
.
Orron is obsessive-compulsive, and doesn't like when things aren't arranged just so. You can disrupt his arrangement to incite a gasp from the rest of his crew, and do it again to start a fight.
Quests
All Aboard
: Orron has a reservation on Captain
Sedūzo
's ship bound for the
Rauatai Gulf
. You'll have to convince him to change to another ship in order to find passage for
Biha
and her children.
Trivia
Despite being a
Goldpact Knight
, Orron's actual
Paladin
subclass is
Kind Wayfarers
.

.
Background
A middle-aged Kuaru woman raises her brows in question when you approach, her hands too full with braided ropes of dried reeds to greet you properly.

Nedunga
how to make rugs. Although housing the castes together has been stressful, Osauro found a new friend - and learned that her culture need not separate the castes by default.

CRW_Erol_of_Levi

bec8676c-1658-484f-a894-a496d3ad7a2c
Oswald
(also known as
Erol of Levi
) is a mentioned-only character in
Pillars of Eternity
, and a character and recruitable
crew member
in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
.
Background
Erol is an elderly
Aedyran
scholar, traveller, explorer, and veteran of the
War of Defiance
(for Dyrwood).
He was among the first of the Aedyran colonists to set foot in the
Dyrwood
. When it became evident that the Dyrwood intended to revolt, he took their side in the War of Defiance, and fought against his country of birth, alongside his friend
Admeth Hadret
.
After the war, in the early days of Dyrwoodan independence from Aedyr, Erol founded
The Goose and Fox
inn in
Defiance Bay
, as a place where kith of all backgrounds could gather and hash out the issues facing their new country. Although Erol prided himself on encouraging fair-mindedness and civil debate, he eventually found himself on the wrong side of an argument with the wrong thayn. His disappearance a few days later was widely speculated, with some claiming it was the work of a thayn, with others claiming he had been killed on his travels. Erol realized that discretion is the better part of valor and skipped town before things got ugly.
Since the betrayal of his homeland 150 years prior, Erol had drawn the ire of the Empire and its agents in
The Steel Garrote
, who were relentlessly hunting him down for his 'grave' transgression. Thus, with the money he made from his inn ventures, he fled to the
Deadfire Archipelago
, where he assumed the name "Oswald".
While in the Deadfire, he began to accumulate a sizable debt to house
Kahn
(a descendant of his friend, Admeth) in the services of a courtesan
Aenalys
in
The Wild Mare
. After absconding with her couple thousand pires, eventually the Steel Garrote caught up him, and he was captured and held on trial by its members, accused of oathbreaking.
Interactions
This character is a potential
crew member
of
The Defiant
.
Novice Navigator
Novice Helmsman
Personality: Chatty, Drunkard
0
per day, +1 water consumption
This character is
involved in
quests
.
Lost Dues in Good Faith
Quests
Lost Dues in Good Faith
: Oswald skipped out on his loan and Kahn wants him found.
Trivia
Erol began his travels in 2662.
Items referencing Erol include
Bartender's Ring
,
Erol's Ring
, and
Oswald's Journal
.
Erol has a painting on the wall of
The Goose and Fox
in his honor. His sudden disappearance roused much speculation amongst the patrons of the inn.
Behind the scenes
Erol of Levi
is named after NeoGAF staff member "EviLore" (of which Erol of Levi is a rough anagram).
The Goose and Fox
is a backer reward for the members of NeoGAF, who contributed $5,000 during the crowdfunding campaign.
Gallery
Oswald's crew portrait

is a character in

The Hole
during
A Sinking Feeling
, and later in the

Hunched on his hands and knees, quivering and drenched in sweat, the pirate lets out a pain-filled groan.

Ponamu Bird-Scorned
is a character in
Pillars of Eternity
(with the
Deadfire Pack
) and
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire

Scalawags Pack
).
Background
An aumaua who has been shipwrecked on his way to Defiance Bay, his hair matted and once-bright clothes in ruins. Equally ruined is his face, a hatching of thin scars crossed by broader wounds. He was part of a crew from the
Deadfire Archipelago
, trafficking goods to Defiance Bay, when a storm cast his ship on the stones of the Compass.
He can be found in
Anslög's Compass
, slightly northwest of
Ranga
, on the path to get to her camp.
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
After the Watcher's defeat of Thaos, Ponamu returned to the Deadfire, picking up his trade of a boatswain.

Rabyuna
is a character in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
.
Background
A fire godlike woman polishes a pair of stocks, tending to them with the fondness of a mother for her favorite child.
The room is dim, illuminated only by the glow of her steel-forged skin. Her eyes burn with the light of Magran's fire.
Rabyuna reached her position through perseverance and effort. She teaches others the same, helping them find the strength they need to face the world as a thinking, feeling creature.

Rakara
is a character in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
.
Background
A gaunt Roparu woman grabs for your leg. She paws at you with a weak grip, fingers bone-thin and trembling.
A gaunt aumaua woman with irises as green as the sea. Known only as "Beggar", Rakara is one of many nameless Roparu who suffer in silence beneath the heels of the Mataru of
Huana
. She is on the verge of starvation, reduced to begging for scraps in the streets of the Gullet.
Interactions
This character is
involved in
quests
.
Food for Thought
Delver's Row
This character has
other interactions
.
You can talk to her to learn that
Enoi
is the informal leader of the Roparu in the Gullet.
You are presented with a number of options, some of which are only available once:
Crouch down to ask her name.
Give her
5
for something to eat (Minor Positive reputation with
The Gullet
), though she returns your coin to you.
Give her some food (
Glazed Chops
,
Shark Meat
,
Pork
,
Forbidden Flesh Pie
,
Hardtack
,
Rice
, or
Koīki Fruit
) (
Benevolent
, Minor Positive reputation with
The Gullet
) to keep her from dying. She dies if you talk to her again without giving her food.
Kick her (
Cruel
, Major Negative reputation with
The Gullet
)
Quests
Food for Thought
: She is among the roparu you are helping during the course of the quest.
Delver's Row
: You can ask her how you might get to Delver's Row. She points you towards
Enoi
, and
Fyrna
(only if you gave her food).
Behind the scenes
The game has an incorrect portrait set for Rakara, using a red-eyed aumaua instead.

Background

.

c0a501ef-16cc-49dc-8517-76792fce5ff8
Remaro
is a character in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
.
Background
Remaro is a veteran captain of the Príncipi sen Patrena, recently accused of mutiny by the highest authorities of the faction, such as they are.
Captain Aeldys
has put a price on his head, demanding that he be brought back - preferably dead.
Serafen
, who owes Remaro a tremendous debt after he saved him from
Malnaj
's excesses during his time as
The Sorcerer'
s surgeon and then captain, is naturally skeptical of the accusations and wants to learn the truth.
Remaro abandoned the Príncipi after the influx of new blood split the organization in half - and the discovery that the old blood wasn't much better. Captain Bastian of
the Sorcerer
was a slaver, hunting down ships carrying slaves only to resell them at
Crookspur
for a profit. Remaro confronted the captain and it went poorly, resulting in a mutiny and then Remaro turning his guns on the slaver ships.  He then fled to Neketaka, trading
The Sorcerer
for an elven clipper in
Neketaka
, then making his way northwest, gunning for an exit from the archipelago, towards the Eastern Reach or the Living Lands - on the far side of Eora.
Interactions
This character is
involved in
quests
.
A Sorcerer and a Gentleman
Quests
A Sorcerer and a Gentleman
: Remaro is the goal of Serafen's quest, although the cipher might not like what he learns in the process.

Rinco
is a character in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
.
Background
The figure in the bed is a young Vailian man. The first thing you notice is that he seems to have been severely beaten. One eye is nearly swollen shut, and where his skin is revealed it is a patchwork of livid bruises.
He groans and winces as he props himself up, glaring up at you with one good eye.
Rinco had the misfortune of coming across
Mokeha
, a local Mataru, who took a liking to the money in his pocket. His night of good luck ended as she pummeled him senselessly, then made off with his pouch.
Torri
, Rinco's son, is keeping him company while he recovers. Rinco's wife, Zaneta, is a researcher at the Engwithan Dig Site.
Interactions
This character
starts
quests
.
Burning Bridges
This character has
other interactions
.
A
godlike
or
island aumaua
Watcher has unique introductory dialogue with Rinco.
Quests
Burning Bridges
: Rinco asks you to recover his money.
Companion reactivity
When first talking to Rinco by his bedside:
Aloth
:
"Reminds me of a time Iselmyr got mouthy with a Rauataian mercenary." He leans close, murmuring to you.
Edér
:
"I know exactly how he feels. I've beat up a lot of folks just the same way."
Xoti
:
"You look like you already got a foot in the grave." She thumbs the cage of her lantern thoughtfully.
(Only if
The Lantern of Gaun
has not yet been completed)
After asking what happened to him:
Serafen
:
"Everyone tells tales of the kraken and the ravagers, but I've long said the aumaua be the true natural danger of the Deadfire."
Serafen:
He winks at Maia.
(If Maia is in the party)
Serafen:
"Meaning no offense to yourself, cap." He grins.
(If the Watcher is an
island aumaua
)

Rust
is a character in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
.
Background
He lightly traces a finger across the hilt of an emerald-encrusted stiletto hidden within the folds of a dark, leather tunic. His narrowed eyes seem to dance in the magical light as the gemstone pulses with a caustic glow.
Rust is an assassin for hire plying his craft in the shadier corners of the Row.
Interactions
This character is
involved in
quests
.
Harsh Medicine
The Cornett's Call
Quests
Harsh Medicine
: He can point you towards
Ernezzo
. You can also hire his services to take out either
The Spindle Man
for
600
or Ernezzo for
300
(only if you have spoken to The Spindle Man about beforehand).
The Cornett's Call
: For
800
, Rust can be asked to acquire the
Cornett of Waves
from
Takano
. For
1,000
, he will do so without killing Takano. Either way, you'll have to wait a day for him to complete the task.
Trivia
Rust is an especially high level character for his location, considering the "expected" level of the area is level 6. Other NPC's in this area are around levels 4-6.
If attacked, and (Presumably) not killed in time, he'll say "Enough!" while teleporting away with a smoke bomb, and, leave the Delver's Row with an injured walking animation.

Ruāsare
is a character in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
.
Background
The broad-shouldered woman on the throne lifts her gaze to meet yours. White face paint adds a grim aspect to her stoic demeanor. Smoldering braziers fill the air with oppressive heat, but she sits at ease.
The ranga of the Wahaki is a powerful, spirited woman who despises the foreigners encroaching on Huana lands - and a descendant of the ranga that burned
Thaos
alive when he tried to pull the same trick he did on the Glanfathans on the Wahaki.
Interactions
This character is
involved in
quests
.
A Shrewd Proposition
The Painted Masks
Quests
A Shrewd Proposition
: She is a target for the slavers. She can be killed by poisoning the koiki fruit in her bedchambers. The unique spear
Kahua Hozi
can then be looted from her.
The Painted Masks
: You can read her soul to discover more about
Thaos
' encounter with the tribe.

PAGE: Rynhaedr
CATEGORIES: Beast of Winter characters
URL: https://pillarsofeternity.fandom.com/wiki/Rynhaedr
======================================================================

Rynhaedr
Upload image
Biography and appearance
Game
Beast of Winter
Race
Pale
elf
Gender
Female
Culture
The White that Wends
Statistics
Class
Fighter
Gameplay
Location
The Shattered Passage
Quests
Death's Depthless Dominion
Rynhaedr
is a character in
Beast of Winter
.
Background
A native of the
White that Wends
, Rynhaedr was a naturally curious and inquisitive child brought up in the faith of her ancestors. Routinely violating the rules set down by the elders and suffering canings for it, she prowled the desolate, snowy wilds on her own, without a companion. Though all suspected she would fall to
Rymrgand
or his Beast, she prevailed and eventually joined the ranks of the gandhur. Asked specifically to join the temple guards at the
Temple of Decline
, Rynhaedr accepted the duty, though her heart yearned for the frigid homeland.
Still, she did her duty and became Rymrgand's champion. Her life on Eora came to an end when
Neriscyrlas
, a powerful
dragon
seeking to dominate the
Deadfire Archipelago
, attacked the temple to gain access to the White Void through the Vydmath, so that she could retrieve any of the immensely powerful relics disposed of within the Maw. Blasting through the defenses of the temple, she managed to make it all the way to the Temple and the breach. Rynhaedr sacrificed herself, opening a conduit through her body so that the Void could consume the dragon and protect Rymrgand's domain.
That was over four hundred years ago, when Aedyr was still young. Since then, she has been battling Neriscyrlas across the White Void, trying to complete her duty to Rymrgand - and failing, repeatedly.
Interactions
This character is
involved in
quests
.
Death's Depthless Dominion
Quests
Death's Depthless Dominion
: Rynhaedr aids the player in finding the dragon.
Behind the scenes
She is voiced by Carolin Stoltz
References

Sanza
is a character in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
and
Avowed
.
Background
The premiere cartographer of
Neketaka
, Sanza is a workaholic who literally sleeps in his office while working on his maps. Sanza is excitable and possibly a little hyper, but there's no denying that he is an excellent specialist in his field. He is also very fond of his dog Kaleb, who hogs all the blankets.
In
Avowed
, Sanza is in
Dawnshore
. He initially appears to the East of the Ivona's Threshold
Party Camp
. Later, he can be found in
Paradis
' hightown, in Sanza's Emporium.
Interactions
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
This character is a
merchant
.
Sells: Maps of Deadfire and grimoires, including the
Snakeskin Grimoire
. Also sells the
spyglass
and plenty of lore books, including the books pointing you in the direction of the various
Mega Boss Battles
.
This character
starts
quests
.
Mapping the Archipelago: Port Maje
Mapping the Archipelago: West Wakara Reef
Mapping the Archipelago: Razai Passage
Mapping the Archipelago: Tikawara
Mapping the Archipelago: The Burning Shoals
This character has
other interactions
.
If you attack his dog
Kaleb
, Sanza says
"My sweet Kaleb! You- you monster!"
Despite mentioning so, Sanza does not sell any actual maps in his store.
Quests
Mapping the Archipelago
: This series of quests takes you all over the Deadfire to map the uncharted islands - and name them.
After completing all of the map quests, Sanza rewards you with
7,000
and 10x
Forgetful Night
, asking you to return later when his book is complete. Upon returning (although you can just talk to him immediately after), he hands you your very own copy of
The Explorer's Guide to the Deadfire Archipelago
.
Avowed
This character
starts
quests
.
Mapping the Living Lands: Dawnshore
Mapping the Living Lands: Emerald Stair
Mapping the Living Lands: Galawain's Tusks
Mapping the Living Lands: Shatterscarp
Behind the scenes
A seemingly unused cutscene exists where Sanza is mid-dialogue with a street urchin when you enter:
"Hm, yes, well, next time- ah, next time you will not give me a coin purse reeking of rat piss, understand? Or I'll charge you twice the rat. Ah, rate! Twice the rate."
"Now, if that's all, I wish you a good day. Thank you for your, ah, distinguished patronage. Do come again. Perhaps with silvers.
"Give them a spit shine, at least. That's a good lad."
He was voiced by
Andres Williams.

Savia
is a character in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
.
Background
The watch commander looks up at you after her listless greeting, and you notice that she has a dark bruise around one eye.
She grimaces, but does not turn away.
Savia might be the watch commander, but the shortage of capable hands forced her to do the dirty work herself. This bruise is the result of her showing too much courtesy to
Rum-Dumb Riggere
, who used the opportunity to punch her in the face while being dragged off to jail.
However, her biggest concern is keeping the peace in the wake of the flooding across Port Maje.
Ilari
, a particularly notorious little ganger, is busy looting the flooded parts of the city with impunity while the guards are stretched thin.
Interactions
This character
starts
quests
.
Restoring Order
The Drunk Sailor
Quests
Restoring Order
: She requests your aid in pacifying
Ilari
and his crew.
The Drunk Sailor
: She keeps watch of
Rum-Dumb Riggere
, and needs to be dealt with to secure his freedom.

Sigilmaster Auranic
is a character and mega boss in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
. She is the third mega boss added to the game, in the update
Mega Boss - Sigilmaster Auranic
.
Background
This traveler's guide is circulated for the benefit of newcomers to the Deadfire Archipelago. One passage stands out:
"Sigilmaster Auranic is ON THE LOOSE. She was sentenced for planting DEADLY sigils in populated areas, and affected her escape with nothing more than a stone game piece and an inkwell.
Trust in the authorities and make NO ATTEMPT to apprehend her. She will have flanked herself in sigils powerful enough to EXPLODE unwary visitors on the spot.
The Deadfire Visitor's Preservation Society takes no responsibility for harm inflicted by knowing ignorance of the risks, and every effort has been made to keep travelers AWAY from the following coordinates: 4° 50' S 67° 31' E."
A map of Auranic's position is marked off with a wax seal in the shape of a skull. It points toward an underwater cave far to the northeast.
Encounters
Briny Grotto
in
Ofecchia Channel
Notes
The obelisks surrounding the sigilmaster all have Globe of Invulnerability, which to no surprise makes them invulnerable to your attacks. Thankfully they cannot attack you or cast spells while in this state. In order to make them attack, the sigilmaster casts Sigil Assault on the obelisks, one at a time. This removes the invulnerability and allows the obelisks to attack for 172 seconds, during which they will repeatedly cast a specific ability.
Each of the sigilmaster's obelisks has the following stats:
60 All Defenses, 10 Base Armor, Immune to Slash and Piercing
Each of the obelisks casts the following spells (from the bottom left, clockwise)
Obelisk of Wrath:
Chain Lightning
, chained shock damage
Obelisk of Terror:
Ryngrim's Enervating Terror
,
terrifying
your party.
Obelist of Mystery: Casts 5x
Tayn's Chaotic Orb
repeatedly at 3.0 sec intervals.
Obelisk of Force: Casts 5x
Minoletta's Minor Missiles
Obelisk of Cleansing:
Arcane Cleanse
, -1000 sec duration of beneficial effects.

Sissak
is a character in
The Forgotten Sanctum
.
Background
A tall, spindly vithrack stands before you. Its carapace is dull and gray, but the figure is no less menacing for its advanced age.
Sissak is the overseer of the wardens and caretakers of the Collections wing of the Halls Obscured. He and the Oracle have a simple, but profitable deal: In return for a never-ending supply of food and peace for the vithrack colony, Sissak's underlings kill kith intruders.

and

as a reward for finding the contract.

will no longer be hostile. In addition,

in the party, their reactivity to the Watcher passing one of the above skill checks will cause the dialogue to end prematurely and you will not receive

======================================================================
PAGE: St. Waidwen
CATEGORIES: Beast of Winter characters
URL: https://pillarsofeternity.fandom.com/wiki/St._Waidwen
======================================================================

St. Waidwen
Biography and appearance
Game
Beast of Winter
Race
Savanna human
Gender
Male
Faction
Readceras
Gameplay
Location
The Bridge Ablaze
Quests
The Bridge Ablaze (quest)
“
Did they expect a dozen to stand against the dawn?
”
~
Waidwen at the Battle of Halgot Citadel
St. Waidwen
was a human farmer, transformed into a living incarnation of
Eothas
and was the first and only 'Divine King' of the
Divine Kingdom of Readceras
.
Background
During the economic downturn, a local farmer named Waidwen started to deliver speeches in the town square. Such activity would normally have been overlooked by the local government, but people listened to his ravings. No one could decide if he was brilliant or mad, but his words struck a chord in the hearts of the devout and those affected by the failure of the vorlas crop. The farmer himself took no credit for the content of his speeches, claiming  that Eothas visited him at night (taking the form of the Dawnstars) and imparted the divine message directly into his soul.
Waidwen was nobody before that, a simple farmer who was raised a devout Eothasian by his parents, who could never quite tame his inquisitive mind. Waidwen wondered about many forbidden subjects, such as the world without the gods and whether it was truly fair to offer thanks to the gods for the work of
their
, kith hands. His doubts were met with violence from his pious father, who was more interested in piety than parenting. Even on his death bed, consumed by the Vorlas Cough, his father stood by his faith, demanding to know if his son honored the gods. He never apologized. To Waidwen, his father's death was essentially liberation.
He tilled the vorlas fields, taking his meager harvest to town and selling it, while watching countless criminals sentenced and executed. When Eothas came to him one day in the fields, he was about to finish and head home. The god offered him a choice, to rebuild an empire - and Waidwen accepted.
Aedyran reaction
According to Eothas, the people of Readceras were being punished for their lack of piety and the devotion they misplaced in the Aedyran governor. Authorities faced a difficult choice.  Imprisoning him could incite a rebellion. If they acted impartial, then antiestablishment notions and religious fervor threatened to infect the minds of the people. As such, they attempted to discredit the man. The town guard seized Waidwen in the middle of his most widely attended speech, erected a pillory, and restrained the emaciated farmer. An enforcer read the list of Waidwen’s crimes, which encompassed a broad range of shaming accusations from cruel statements to a child, through animancy, to public indecency, sexual congress with a cean gŵla, and venereal disease.
A brief hearing followed proclamations of guilt and a sentence of thirty lashes. The crowd protested, but Waidwen placated them with his full consent to carry out the punishment. After the first five lashes, the enforcement officer hesitated and consulted with others on the dais.  Waidwen never screamed. Every bite of the whip opened another strip of light from the farmer’s skin. When the anxious colonial secretary called for the punishment to stop prematurely, Waidwen demanded more. According to the Eothasians in attendance, his voice sounded “not his own.”
As the officer delivered the final lash, a brilliant, white light exploded from Waidwen’s back and engulfed his head in a flaming crown. He stood up, the chains falling from his arms in molten pieces. With the full attention of the colony, the thing that was Waidwen finished his speech. He called for the people to rise up—not as a mob, but as pilgrims tasked with delivering the bloody will of the divine.
Divine Kingdom
After the Miracle of the Verdant Vorlas, Waidwen quickly gathered followers, drawn to the stories of Eothas's miraculous prophet. His power grew. Within days, Waidwen had gained enough support that he confronted the imperial governor. Assisted by a collection of knights and nobles who had been swayed to his cause, he marched on the capitol city. The governor was allowed to live, but was forced to abdicate power and leave the colony. This was not from any understanding or easy acquiescence from the governor, but because of what happened when Waidwen entered the governor's palace. As Waidwen approached the governor, according to accounts, his body turned into something that was no longer human. His flesh became luminescent and his head transformed into pure, blinding light.
The governor, knowing there was no way he could oppose an avatar of Eothas, relinquished his power. The people then asked Waidwen to lead the colony. He accepted, earning him the name ‘Divine King’ of Readceras. Waidwen's rule was virtually uncontested. Initially this was because everyone was awed that a god had chosen to manifest himself and lead his people. This changed as Waidwen began punishing the allies of the old empire and the ‘poison on the world’ - what he considered corrupt churches or church leaders of Eothas. Scrutiny escalated and soon worshippers of Eothas were also being punished for mere perceptions of heresy. Members of other religions were also added to the list of the persecuted for following different faiths. This caused large segments of the population to flee Readceras for the Dyrwood, begging for sanctuary. This caused strife between the two nations. The people of the Dyrwood knew that they could not sustain explosive population growth if Waidwen's rule were to continue unchecked. They also feared that his eye would turn from Readceras and land on them next if nothing was done. This was exactly what ultimately happened, and open war broke out as Waidwen moved to spread his dominion into the lands of Dyrwood.
Saint's War
“
Waidwen's head was a beam of light.
”
~
The Watcher to Edér
Waidwen personally led many of the battles during the war, exhibiting extraordinary supernatural powers. He seemed virtually untouchable on the battlefield, able to burn or even disintegrate his enemies with beams of blinding, white light. With a god on his side and possibly, as some said, inhabiting him, he was thought to be indestructible. A flanking maneuver through
The White March
mountains, enabled by the abject surrender of
Cold Morn
in the face of overwhelming odds and the sacking of
Mercy Vale
left Dyrwood's morale in shambles, setting a grim tone for the rest of the campaign.
The victorious streak lasted until the Battle of
Halgot Citadel
. The people of the Dyrwood knew they would lose the war if they could not at least slow Waidwen down. Engineers, priests of Magran, and a few others, working in secret (some say with Magran’s direct help), developed a weapon they hoped would be able to stop a god. Twelve feet in diameter and filled with a variety of chemical and magical explosives, the bomb was rolled under Evon Dewr Bridge. Part of the foundation was excavated in order to allow them to embed the bomb in the bridge itself, ensuring its total concealment.
Twelve Dyrwoodan men and women volunteered to stage an ambush at the bridge to keep Waidwen on it until the bomb could be detonated. The battle was short, bloody, and ultimately final. ‘The Dozen’ (as they came to be known) were able to delay Waidwen on the bridge. The bomb detonated, killing Waidwen, the four Dyrwoodan volunteers still alive at that time, and over fifty Readceran soldiers marching on the front line with Waidwen. It was at that moment The Saint's War ended. The remaining Readceran forces were easy to rout. Even though they had more than enough men and equipment to finish the siege, their leader - previously thought invincible - had just vanished in a rain of metal and stone. Panic set in and the Dyrwoodan troops sent them away with ease.
From that point on, the bomb was known by the name ‘Godhammer.’ It even worked its way into everyday conversation. "As sure as Godhammer ended the Saint's War," came to be a standard phrase to express unequivocal certainty. Less certain is the fate of Eothas, who has not spoken to his followers since the explosion of the bomb and is presumed by most to be dead. There has never been another documented explosion of such magnitude, and efforts to locate the engineers and clergy responsible for the bomb have been entirely fruitless (they were wiped out by
Magran
, except for one,
Durance
).
The eventual failure of the conflict left Readceras a modest refuge for devout Eothasians. Strictly imposed faith and discipline led to the country’s reputation as a counterpoint to the progress and innovation of Dyrwood. Its people live in close-knit communities with no lack of oversight, their policies determined by societal and religious judgment as opposed to mortal law.
Many Eothasians fled to Readceras or the
Aedyr Empire
following the end of the war, as purges of Eothasians began across the Dyrwood, only intensifying with the advent of
Waidwen's Legacy
.
Interactions
This character is
involved in
quests
.
The Bridge Ablaze
Quests
The Bridge Ablaze
Trivia
St. Waidwen is based on legends of
Hans Böhm
, the Drummer of Niklashausen.
Waidwen was written by Paul Kirsch and painted by Matt Hansen.
The game asset version of the portrait is very small, the larger version was shared by the artist himself, Matt Hansen.

is a character in

.
Background
The lighthouse is quiet but for soft, sibilant whispers. There's a repetitive, incantatory quality to them.
Yet as you cross the threshold, an old nāga with skin like cracked leather breaks off. He swivels to face you, baring one broken fang.
Sugaan is a naga shaman leading the incursion into Hasongo, to defend the luminous adra pillars from Rauataians, convinced that their disruption of the
tree of the gods
will make them punish them with another extinction event, wiping out most life across the archipelago. As heir to the collective knowledge of the naga folk, he understands history and its processes better than most kith.

Jacob Harker

The King's Coffin

Takano
is a character in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
.
Background
An older Mataru man stands ringed by younger Huana - apprentices or pupils, it seems. His robes shimmer with quartz beading, and his perfume announces his presence from across the room.
Yet beneath his finery, he looks like a fighter gone to seed. Disused muscles flop from his arms, and flab pads him like so many layers of silk.
He looks up and notices you.
Takano is well-known for his hospitality in
Neketaka
. Among Vailians, however, he is better known for the sizable debts his lifestyle has incurred. His only chance, he believes, is intimidating visitors, as the only thing of truly great worth he has is a conch hidden deep in one of his trunks, a gift from the queen...
Interactions

======================================================================
PAGE: Tayn
CATEGORIES: The Forgotten Sanctum characters
URL: https://pillarsofeternity.fandom.com/wiki/Tayn
======================================================================

Tayn
Upload image
Biography and appearance
Game
The Forgotten Sanctum
Race
Human
Gender
Male
Faction
Circle of Archmagi
Statistics
Class
Wizard
Gameplay
Location
Temple of Revelation
Quests
Annotated History
Under Observation
A Shout in the Dark
“
What, the prospect of sending a mountain of eyes and tentacles to wrestle Eothas isn't enticing enough for you?" Tayn chuckles softly. "Wouldn't it be boring to let a body like that moulder and rot? I think we can do better. I think Eora deserves better. Even if it knocks over a castle or two, I think the fun will justify the cost.
”
Tayn
is one of the archmages of
Eora
, appearing  in
The Forgotten Sanctum
.
Background
An eccentric Aedyran archmage, Tayn is known for his power and chaotic personality. While a majority of his work is secreted away (likely due to being catastrophic failures), Tayn himself remains on the loose, bringing his own brand of craziness to
Eora
. Although at odds with his more formal colleagues, especially
Llengrath
, whom he consistently antagonizes by using the diminutive Llen, Tayn retains a seat on the council of archmages. Unlike
Concelhaut
, he is affable and mostly harmless, after all - at least, as long as his more mature colleagues keep an eye on him.
Aloth
describes Tayn as an insult to the very concept of scholarship, which is mostly due to the fact that his rise to archmage was unorthodox. Tayn received a brilliant education courtesy of his father, who donated to the finest colleges in Aedyr, earning his son several free degrees until he actually found something he was good at. Once he found it, he latched on to it and perfected his art, without ever challenging himself beyond it. It granted him refinement, a place among the Circle, and the disappointment of his father: He always wanted an archmage in the family, but Tayn promptly dropped the surname later in life.
His work ethic is also completely different from the rest of the colleagues. Tayn relies entirely on raw, unvarnished instinct, rather than careful study, leading to the creation of spells and inventions that are as chaotic and unpredictable as their maker. His proudest (and first) achievement is
Tayn's Chaotic Orb
, which was released to applause, then just used as an (un)reliable offensive spells. Other creations are
Tayn's Gratitude
,
Tayn's Chaotic Missiles
, and
Tayn's Scroll of Righteous Awakening
, designed to reinstate memories in the hollowed-out people imprisoned in the Collections beneath The Black Isles... Completely at random.
His fellow mages hold a variety of opinions of him.
Llengrath
detests him as an insult to the profession,
Citzal
is, apparently, Tayn's pen pal (although he thinks the archmage is an orlan clockmaker), while
Minoletta
once pushed Tayn into a snake pit.
Ninagauth
mostly keeps to himself, while
Kalakoth
once allegedly shouted into Tayn's face so loud they both passed out.
Arkemyr
is, well, Arkemyr, to Tayn and everyone else.
Ryngrim
is the object of Tayn's intense friendship campaign, while
Maura
, apparently, is the sole mage who's actually on good terms with Tayn. According to him, at least.
Interactions
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
This character
starts
quests
.
A Shout in the Dark
This character is
involved in
quests
.
Annotated History
Under Observation
Quests
Annotated History
,
Under Observation
: In answering the call of
Maura
, he and Llengrath suggest that the Watcher spearhead the exploration of the ruins beneath the Black Isles that contain Wael's titanic body.
A Shout in the Dark
: Tayn wants the Watcher to liberate the prisoners of Collections by randomly reinserting their memories. Wonderful.

other interactions

Location

The Beast of Winter
is a character in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
in
Beast of Winter
.
Background
The Beast of Winter is the avatar and most primal expression of the god Rymrgand, which takes the form of a massive, upright-standing aurochs. In keeping with Rymrgand's portfolio of death as a destructive and final ending, the Beast is synonymous with merciless execution. He symbolizes sorrow and the inevitability of stillness at the end of all things. Inevitability seems to be the only thing the Beast actively cares about, where any effort to stifle or delay one's destruction is seen as prey to be chased down and beaten under the Beast's frozen hooves.
Interactions
This character is
involved in
quests
.

: The Beast is confronted at the end of the quest, allowing for a combat-heavy and consequence-free escape from the Void.

Thorel
is a character in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
.
Background
The rotund and cheerful Thorel is the owner of
The Kraken's Eye
, the biggest - and only - tavern in the whole of
Port Maje
. The recent storm is resulting in lots of profit form him, but also denies rooms to anyone beyond those already booked. He's also a font of information on what's going on in the town, especially when it relates to the patrons of his establishment.
He named the tavern after his greatest triumph during his seafaring years: Defeating a
kraken
that has already destroyed seven ships and ate their crews. As the helmsman of the ship that took the beast down, he was awarded its eye by his captain - it's his greatest treasure.
Interactions
This character is a
merchant
.
Sells: Food, drink, and rooms
This character
starts
quests
.

This character has
other interactions
.

Ale
out of sympathy for your troubles at
Vilario's Rest
.
When asked how he can tell you came from the shipwreck, a
coastal aumaua
or
godlike
Watcher will receive a unique response.
Stealing the
Kraken's Eye
eye in plain view will cause Thorel to demand you return it. You can say you were just looking and return it, or pocket the eye, which will cause him to become hostile. These options are skipped entirely if you killed Galain without starting the quest
The Better Man
.
If you stole the
Kraken's Eye
from the wall, he mentions this when asked about the tavern's namesake, and also as his introductory dialogue after completing
The Better Man
.

Tipa
is a character in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
.
Background
Sister to
Weto
, Tipa is adamant about upholding their Huana traditions and rejecting the aid of the Rauataians at
Sayuka
, after a series of storms wiped out their village and food supply. Tipa fears that accepting the aid - and the Rauataian way of life - will spell the end of Huana culture, caste divisions and all. She especially abhors the Rauataians forcing
unity
and
equality
among the Huana by quartering them all in one longhouse.
Interactions
This character has
other interactions
.
You can gain Minor Positive Reputation with the
Huana
by agreeing with her.

He's been tracked to an island east of Magran's Teeth where he and his pet lion are likely to defend against fortune-seekers.

Udyne
is a character in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
.
Background
A venerable elf sits beside the water, her creased and spotted skin slightly flushed by the heat. Numerous scars mar her skin on face and torso alike. Her eyes open, and their sharp gaze focuses on you.
Udyne is ancient even by elven standards. She fought in the
Broken Stone War
two centuries past, seeking glory in battle while protecting Aedyran colonists. she considers herself lucky, as despite going up against Glanfathan mind hunters, she survived where her companions were slaughtered body and soul. Her career took a turn for the worse when they were visiting a farmer near Log Home. Treated to a feast, they were set upon by Glanfathans, who lured them outside by riling the animals. First came the arrows from sceltrfolc, killing two of her compatriots, then they were rushed by a troop of orlan ciphers. By the end of the battle, only Udyne survived and even then, she was clutching her innards to prevent them from spilling out. The farmer helped her, sewing her up and nourishing until she could walk.
Udyne continued to fight, this time in the
War of the Black Trees
and then in the
War of Defiance
, on the imperial side. After Aedyr was forced to concede defeat, she traveled north. At this point, the wounds started to affect her general health (eighteen arrows and nine stab wounds tend to do that). She sought refuge in drinking, svef, and now luminous adra baths to dull the agony.
Interactions
This character is
involved in
quests
.
A Sorcerer and a Gentleman
Quests
A Sorcerer and a Gentleman
: Udyne can guide you to
Remaro
.

Vektor
is a character, merchant, and a recruitable
crew member
in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
.
Background
The dwarf fans himself with a dishrag. His face is dark and shiny with exertion. Sweat colors wide crescents on his shirt.
He looks at you like a drowning man would look at dry land.
Vektor is a mountain dwarf from the Republics, descended from
Pargrunen
immigrants. At the present, he's a member of the Vailian Trading Company sent as part of a larger contingent to
Tikawara
, in order to exploit the
luminous adra
deposits at
Poko Kohara ruins
. His team received a ducal welcome at first, until Anaharu, the local priest, voiced his objections and turned the local opinion against the Vailians. Although no violence happened, they were forced to sleep on their boat - except for Vektor. It seems that the local cuisine doesn't agree with him, leading to nasty runs.
He suspects that the local chieftain gave his team a false lead under the priest's influence, leading them to a horrible fate. As the galley cook, he has few options at his disposal and was left stranded on the dock, waiting for relief to come. It did not come, causing him no small amount of anxiety.
Interactions
This character is a
merchant
.
Sells: A broad variety of supplies, including fine and rare armor pieces, scrolls, the whole nine yards.
This character is a potential
crew member
of
The Defiant
.
Novice Cook
Personality: Chatty, Loyal
This character
starts
quests
.
The Storms of Poko Kohara
This character has
other interactions
.
Has unique interactions with
Maia
and
Tekehu
.
Wares
Notable wares include:

Vessatraz
is a character in
The Forgotten Sanctum
.
Background
The vithrack floats before you, her mandibles shivering slightly as she examines you with unmoving eyes like gems set into her head.
Vessatraz has managed to stockpile a small collection of odds and ends from around the facility - crafting much of it herself - and will happily exchange them with the Watcher. Despite the colony's enslavement, she has been to the surface before, supposedly in search of more provisions.
Interactions

Watūri
is a character in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
.
Background
A member of the privileged Mataru caste, Waturi is absolutely disgusted at the fact that he has to share a longhouse with the lowly Roparu - despite the fact that he claimed the nicest quarters for himself. It seems that prejudices die hard.
Waturi is concerned for the safety of his prized possession, his grandmother's war hammer (which he keeps locked in the chest in the corner), and fears that if he were to display it, the Reparu in the longhouse might attempt to steal it.
Interactions
This character has
other interactions
.
He carries
Mataru's Key
, which can be used on the nearby chest to obtain a
Superb War Hammer
.
Watūri does react to stealing the war hammer.

Weto
is a character in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
.
Background
A broad-shouldered man with a long, jagged scar across his brow argues with a woman outside the longhouse. He throws his hands up, about to shout, but the woman cuts him off mid-exclamation.
Weto is the polar opposite of his sister,
Tipa
, who rejects Rauatai. He believes that since the Huana and Rauatai have common ancestors and can complement one another (Huana give land and resources, Rauatai technology and military might), they can forge a new, common culture that's stronger than the preceding ones.
Interactions
This character has
other interactions
.
You can gain Minor Positive reputation with the RDC if you agree with him.

GUID

Ymir
is a character in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
.
Background
The dancer turns to greet you, a coy smile tugging at his lips.
He's short for an elf, but no less graceful for his lacking height. His long face and dark eyes lend him a solemn air, but any hint of gloom is chased away by the wash of color in his cheeks.
Ymir hails from the
Aedyr Empire
and studied in his youth to become an arcane knight. A prank that went awry and killed several people cut these plans short and, even if he claims it was work of his fellow students rather than being involved himself, caused him to flee all the way to
Neketaka
. Ymir still appears to feel remorse for the incident, but moved on and settled on a career where he makes his own hours, meets fascinating people, and earns good money. He calls the Aedyr Empire terribly boring.
Ymir is
Aloth
's acquaintance from school, and is surprised to see Aloth visiting such establishment, although Aloth is quick to declare his preferences haven't changed. Ymir seems to have been romantically interested in Aloth, but Aloth says that he had "confused the poor fellow" during their academy days, followed by a comment from Iselmyr (if she was not suppressed), suggesting that she was the one flirting with Ymir in Aloth's stead. The prank Ymir mentions is presumably the same
animancy
experiment that Aloth tried to tattle on before it was brought to fruition, losing his own favor with the instructors in the process.
Interactions
This character has
other interactions
.
Bringing
Aloth
along results in a unique interaction.
For
150
you can hire his services and receive Ymir's Boon (+1
Constitution
and
Insight
, +2
Reflex
)

Yngfrith

Internal Name
CHA_17_DUN_Yngfrith
GUID
996278ab-b7c2-4599-bd39-454026c3dc99
Yngfrith
is a character in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
.
Background
Yngfrith is the original owner of
Modwyr
, the soulbound blade found beneath Neketaka. She was born a cipher and was sold by her parents to a master animancer, who was working to refine the art of housing souls and thought she would be an asset. She helped create Modwyr, in an act that horrified her so much that she fled into the night with the blade in hand, vowing to fight abuses of animancy.
She joined
Dunryd Row
for a time, fighting animancers... Only to learn that she was becoming like the people she hunted. She fled to the Deadfire, trying to put her past and guilt behind her, but it didn't matter. The shame was within her and ate away at her every day she wandered the Archipelago. Eventually, she threw Modwyr away, hoping that with it, the shame would go away. It didn't.
Interactions
This character has
other interactions
.
Approaching her with
Modwyr
in hand will allow you to confront the two, and learn just why Modwyr wound up in the dump - and if you so decide, reunite the two.
Notes
Yngfrith only appears after reaching soulbound level 4 with Modwyr - "Talk to Yngfrith", and will be located near
Rosanella
's bar in
Radiant Court
.

Zamar
is a character in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
.
Background
The head of the shipyard in Queen's Berth, Zamar is the go-to dwarf when you need your ship fixed. Of course, sometimes clients renege on the agreements, leaving him with a pile of bills and nothing to pay them with. He's also old - very old - and has trouble keeping up with the work.
Interactions
This character is a
merchant
.
Sells: Ships and ship supplies
This character
starts
quests
.
The Shipwright's Plight
This character has
other interactions
.
Dwarves
have unique dialogue with Zamar when first talking to him:
"Glad to see a client eye to eye for a change."
Completing
The Shipwright's Plight
gives a 10% discount on goods at the shipyard.
Quests
The Shipwright's Plight
: He asks you to settle a debt in return for a pay cut or selling the debtor's commission.
Behind the scenes
It was once possible to repair
The Defiant
in dialogue with Zamar for
10,000
(unrelated to
Repair Supplies
), giving you the ability to sail in "deeper waters". This mechanic seems to have been cut and replaced with the
Stranded
quest arc on
Maje Island
.

, west of the VTC HQ, near the cobbler (see below).
Background
This young man appears either to be composing or practicing a tune on his lute. He stops mid-strum, looking up at you with a friendly expression.
Zili is an easy-going kid with an artistic soul, who doesn't want a part of the family's criminal enterprises.
Interactions
This character is
involved in
quests
.
Family Pride
A Bigger Fish
Quests
Family Pride
: Zili Valera can be interrogated to find out about the Valera heist job.
A Bigger Fish
: Zili Valera will recognize the task you have been given, and advise you to send the sailors to him to avoid bloodshed.
Notes
If both
A Bigger Fish
and
Family Pride
are active at the same time, progressing Family Pride first will lock out further dialogue with Zili Valera, preventing the peaceful outcome for A Bigger Fish that involves him.
He will not show up for
A Bigger Fish
until you start
Family Pride
and have talked to
Ezzali Bardatto
about sabotage starting
A Sinking Feeling
.
